The relevant clauses will appear in each\n  1699→ * parameterized join path's joinrestrictinfo list, instead.  ParamPathInfos\n  1700→ * for append relations don't bother with this, either.\n  1701→ *\n  1702→ * ppi_serials is the set of rinfo_serial numbers for quals that are enforced\n  1703→ * by this path.  As with ppi_clauses, it's only maintained for baserels.\n  1704→ * (We could construct it on-the-fly from ppi_clauses, but it seems better\n  1705→ * to materialize a copy.)\n  1706→ */\n  1707→typedef struct ParamPathInfo\n  1708→{\n  1709→\tpg_node_attr(no_copy_equal, no_read, no_query_jumble)\n  1710→\n  1711→\tNodeTag\t\ttype;\n  1712→\n  1713→\tRelids\t\tppi_req_outer;\t/* rels supplying parameters used by path */\n  1714→\tCardinality ppi_rows;\t\t/* estimated number of result tuples */\n  1715→\tList\t   *ppi_clauses;\t/* join clauses available from outer rels */\n  1716→\tBitmapset  *ppi_serials;\t/* set of rinfo_serial for enforced quals */\n  1717→} ParamPathInfo;\n  1718→\n  1719→\n  1720→/*\n  1721→ * Type \"Path\" is used as-is for sequential-scan paths, as well as some other\n  1722→ * simple plan types that we don't need any extra information in the path for.\n  1723→ * For other path types it is the first component of a larger struct.\n  1724→ *\n  1725→ * \"pathtype\" is the NodeTag of the Plan node we could build from this Path.\n  1726→ * It is partially redundant with the Path's NodeTag, but allows us to use\n  1727→ * the same Path type for multiple Plan types when there is no need to\n  1728→ * distinguish the Plan type during path processing.\n  1729→ *\n  1730→ * \"parent\" identifies the relation this Path scans, and \"pathtarget\"\n  1731→ * describes the precise set of output columns the Path would compute.\n  1732→ * In simple cases all Paths for a given rel share the same targetlist,\n  1733→ * which we represent by having path->pathtarget equal to parent->reltarget.\n  1734→ *\n  1735→ * \"param_info\", if not NULL, links to a ParamPathInfo that identifies outer\n  1736→ * relation(s) that provide parameter values to each scan of this path.\n  1737→ * That means this path can only be joined to those rels by means of nestloop\n  1738→ * joins with this path on the inside.  Also note that a parameterized path\n  1739→ * is responsible for testing all \"movable\" joinclauses involving this rel\n  1740→ * and the specified outer rel(s).\n  1741→ *\n  1742→ * \"rows\" is the same as parent->rows in simple paths, but in parameterized\n  1743→ * paths and UniquePaths it can be less than parent->rows, reflecting the\n  1744→ * fact that we've filtered by extra join conditions or removed duplicates.\n  1745→ *\n  1746→ * \"pathkeys\" is a List of PathKey nodes (see above), describing the sort\n  1747→ * ordering of the path's output rows.\n  1748→ *\n  1749→ * We do not support copying Path trees, mainly because the circular linkages\n  1750→ * between RelOptInfo and Path nodes can't be handled easily in a simple\n  1751→ * depth-first traversal.  We also don't have read support at the moment.\n  1752→ */\n  1753→typedef struct Path\n  1754→{\n  1755→\tpg_node_attr(no_copy_equal, no_read, no_query_jumble)\n  1756→\n  1757→\tNodeTag\t\ttype;\n  1758→\n  1759→\t/* tag identifying scan/join method */\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. 3424→\t}\n  3425→}\n  3426→\n  3427→/*\n  3428→ * standard_join_search\n  3429→ *\t  Find possible joinpaths for a query by successively finding ways\n  3430→ *\t  to join component relations into Key Data Structures\n\n#### **Path Node** (Planning-time representation)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:1753`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct Path {\n    NodeTag type;\n    NodeTag pathtype;              // identifies scan/join method (T_SeqScan, T_HashJoin, etc.)\n    RelOptInfo *parent;            // relation this path builds\n    PathTarget *pathtarget;        // output columns and costs\n    ParamPathInfo *param_info;     // parameterization info (for nestloop)\n    \n    bool parallel_aware;\n    bool parallel_safe;\n    int parallel_workers;\n    \n    // Cost estimates\n    Cardinality rows;              // estimated # of result tuples\n    Cost startup_cost;             // cost before fetching any tuples\n    Cost total_cost;               // total cost (assuming all tuples fetched)\n    \n    List *pathkeys;                // sort ordering of output\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Represents one possible way to execute a query. Multiple paths can exist for a single relation, representing different scan methods (seq scan vs index scan) or join orders.\n\n#### **Plan Node** (Execution-time representation)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/plannodes.h:158`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct Plan {\n    NodeTag type;\n    \n    // Cost information from path (copied)\n    Cost startup_cost;\n    Cost total_cost;\n    Cardinality plan_rows;\n    int plan_width;\n    \n    // Execution info\n    int plan_node_id;              // unique ID in plan tree\n    List *targetlist;              // target list to compute\n    List *qual;                    // WHERE clauses to check\n    struct Plan *lefttree;         // outer input plan\n    struct Plan *righttree;        // inner input plan\n    List *initPlan;                // subquery plans\n    \n    // Parameterization\n    Bitmapset *extParam;           // external PARAM_EXEC params\n    Bitmapset *allParam;           // all affecting params\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Represents actual executable instructions for the executor. Contains the same cost info as Path but adds executor-specific information.\n\n#### **RelOptInfo** (Relation information)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:883`\n\n```c\ntypedef struct RelOptInfo {\n    RelOptKind reloptkind;         // BASEREL, JOINREL, UPPERREL, etc.\n    Relids relids;                 // which relations included\n    Cardinality rows;              // estimated # of result rows\n    \n    // Paths for this relation\n    List *pathlist;                // all possible access paths\n    List *partial_pathlist;        // partial (parallel) paths\n    Path *cheapest_startup_path;   // fastest to start returning tuples\n    Path *cheapest_total_path;     // lowest total cost\n    \n    // For base relations\n    Index relid;                   // range table index\n    List *baserestrictinfo;        // restriction clauses\n    List *indexlist;               // available indexes\n    \n    // Materialization info\n    PathTarget *reltarget;         // default output columns\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Stores planning-time information about a relation (base table, join result, or upper-stage result). Contains all possible paths and their costs.\n\n#### **PlannerInfo** (Context for one query level)\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/pathnodes.h:216`\n\n```c\nstruct PlannerInfo {\n    Query *parse;                  // the query being planned\n    PlannerGlobal *glob;           // global state for whole planning\n    \n    // Base relations and join relations\n    RelOptInfo **simple_rel_array;     // base rels indexed by RT index\n    List *join_rel_list;           // all join relations considered\n    List *initial_rels;            // RTEs to be joined\n    \n    // Join search state\n    List **join_rel_level;         // DP state: j-item rels at each level\n    int join_cur_level;            // current DP level\n    \n    // Upper-stage relations\n    List *upper_rels[UPPERREL_FINAL + 1];  // GROUP BY, DISTINCT, ORDER BY, etc.\n    \n    // Various planner state\n    List *eq_classes;              // equivalence classes\n    List *join_info_list;          // special join info\n    List *placeholder_list;        // placeholder variables\n}\n```\n\n**Purpose:** Central planning context, holding all RelOptInfos, equivalence classes, and planning decisions.\n\n#### **Path Subtype Examples:**\n\n**JoinPath** (Abstract base for join paths):\n```c\ntypedef struct JoinPath {\n    Path path;\n    JoinType jointype;             // INNER, LEFT, SEMI, ANTI, etc.\n    bool inner_unique;             // inner rels produce unique matches\n    Path *outerjoinpath;           // outer side\n    Path *innerjoinpath;           // inner side\n    List *joinrestrictinfo;        // join clauses\n}\n```\n\n**NestPath, MergePath, HashPath** - all derive from JoinPath, representing different join methods.\n\n### 5. Path Generation Process (Phase 1)\n\n**Key Functions in `allpaths.c`:**\n\n1. **`make_one_rel()`** - Main entry point for path generation:\n   - Sets up startup cost considerations\n   - Calls `set_base_rel_sizes()` - estimates rows for each base relation\n   - Calls `set_base_rel_pathlists()` - generates access paths\n   - Calls `make_rel_from_joinlist()` - generates join paths\n\n2. **`set_base_rel_pathlists()`** - For each base relation:\n   - Calls `set_rel_pathlist()` which generates:\n     - Sequential scan path via `create_seqscan_path()`\n     - Index scan paths via `create_index_paths()`\n     - Other specialized paths depending on relation type\n\n3. **`make_rel_from_joinlist()`** - Orchestrates join planning:\n   - Recursively processes join tree\n   - Calls `standard_join_search()` for multi-way joins\n\n4. **`standard_join_search()`** - Dynamic programming algorithm:\n   - Uses `join_rel_level[]` to track relations at each DP level\n   - For each level from 2 to N:\n     - Calls `join_search_one_level()` to find all possible N-way joins\n     - For each new join relation, calls `set_cheapest()` to identify the cheapest paths\n   - Returns the final joined relation with multiple alternative paths\n\n**How paths are generated:**\n- `add_path()` adds a path to a relation's pathlist if it's not dominated by existing paths\n- Paths are compared by cost (startup and total)\n- Multiple paths can coexist if they have different performance tradeoffs (e.g., fast startup vs low total cost)\n\n### 6. Plan Creation Process (Phase 2)\n\n**Key Function: `create_plan()`** (line 337 in createplan.c)\n\n1. Calls `create_plan_recurse()` which recursively converts paths to plans\n2. Each Path type has a corresponding function:\n\n```c\nswitch (best_path->pathtype) {\n    case T_SeqScan:\n    case T_IndexScan:\n    case T_IndexOnlyScan:\n    case T_BitmapHeapScan:\n    // ... other scan types\n        plan = create_scan_plan(root, best_path, flags);\n        \n    case T_HashJoin:\n    case T_MergeJoin:\n    case T_NestLoop:\n        plan = create_join_plan(root, (JoinPath *)best_path);\n        \n    case T_Append:\n    case T_MergeAppend:\n    case T_Result:\n    case T_Material:\n    // ... etc\n}\n```\n\n3. For each plan node, conversion includes:\n   - Building the target list (output columns)\n   - Converting path costs to plan costs\n   - Creating sub-plans for inner paths via recursive calls\n   - Setting up qual conditions and parameter info\n\n4. Finally applies:\n   - Target list labeling for result columns\n   - Attaches initPlans (subqueries)\n   - Validates parameter assignments\n\n### 7. Best Path Selection\n\n**Location:** `standard_planner()` lines 437-441\n\n```c\n// Get the final relation with all alternative paths\nfinal_rel = fetch_upper_rel(root, UPPERREL_FINAL, NULL);\n\n// Select the cheapest path based on tuple_fraction\nbest_path = get_cheapest_fractional_path(final_rel, tuple_fraction);\n\n// Convert to executable plan\ntop_plan = create_plan(root, best_path);\n```\n\n- The cheapest path is determined by `get_cheapest_fractional_path()` which considers:\n  - If we need all tuples: minimum total_cost\n  - If we need only some tuples: minimum startup_cost (faster to get first row)\n  - The `tuple_fraction` parameter drives this decision\n\n### 8. Structural Differences: Path vs Plan\n\n| Aspect | Path | Plan |\n|--------|------|------|\n| **Purpose** | Represents possible execution strategies (planning-time) | Represents actual executor instructions (runtime) |\n| **Cost info** | startup_cost, total_cost, rows | Copied from path |\n| **Selection** | Multiple paths exist; best one chosen | Single path selected and converted |\n| **Structure** | Recursive tree via parent RelOptInfo pointers | Recursive tree via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Key differences** | Focuses on cost estimates and ordering | Focuses on executor implementation |\n| **Children** | References via subpath or outer/innerjoinpath | Pointers via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Qualifications** | Implicit in WHERE/JOIN clauses | Explicit in qual lists |\n\n### 9. Important Upper-Level Planning\n\nThe planner also handles upper-level operations after the base join planning:\n\n- **GROUP BY:** `UPPERREL_GROUP_AGG`\n- **DISTINCT:** `UPPERREL_DISTINCT`\n- **ORDER BY:** `UPPERREL_ORDERED`\n- **Set operations:** `UPPERREL_SETOP` (UNION/INTERSECT/EXCEPT)\n- **Window functions:** `UPPERREL_WINDOW`\n\nThese are applied by `grouping_planner()` which generates additional paths for aggregation, sorting, etc., before the final path selection.\n\n### Summary\n\nThe PostgreSQL planner follows a clean two-phase architecture:\n\n1. **Phase 1 (Path Generation):** Explores the search space of possible execution strategies for each relation and join, generating multiple Path nodes that represent different ways to achieve the goal, annotated with cost estimates.\n\n2. **Phase 2 (Plan Creation):** Takes the best Path (minimizing startup or total cost depending on context) and converts it into an executable Plan tree that the executor can run, copying cost information and adding executor-specific details.\n\nThis separation allows the planner to:\n- Consider multiple strategies before committing to one\n- Apply sophisticated optimization rules during path generation\n- Avoid expensive plan conversions for dominated paths\n- Make cost-based decisions about which execution strategy to use"},{"type":"text","text":"agentId: aef8d2fd52f37da11 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)\n<usage>total_tokens: 75714\ntool_uses: 59\nduration_ms: 80372</usage>"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"026159cb-0c93-4594-8106-2a09e233cb62","uuid":"d8fca8d8-7986-4f94-a34e-bb65d3a29b44","tool_use_result":{"status":"completed","prompt":"I need to understand the PostgreSQL planner/optimizer architecture focusing on:\n\n1. For each plan node, conversion includes:\n   - Building the target list (output columns)\n   - Converting path costs to plan costs\n   - Creating sub-plans for inner paths via recursive calls\n   - Setting up qual conditions and parameter info\n\n4. Finally applies:\n   - Target list labeling for result columns\n   - Attaches initPlans (subqueries)\n   - Validates parameter assignments\n\n### 7. Best Path Selection\n\n**Location:** `standard_planner()` lines 437-441\n\n```c\n// Get the final relation with all alternative paths\nfinal_rel = fetch_upper_rel(root, UPPERREL_FINAL, NULL);\n\n// Select the cheapest path based on tuple_fraction\nbest_path = get_cheapest_fractional_path(final_rel, tuple_fraction);\n\n// Convert to executable plan\ntop_plan = create_plan(root, best_path);\n```\n\n- The cheapest path is determined by `get_cheapest_fractional_path()` which considers:\n  - If we need all tuples: minimum total_cost\n  - If we need only some tuples: minimum startup_cost (faster to get first row)\n  - The `tuple_fraction` parameter drives this decision\n\n### 8. Structural Differences: Path vs Plan\n\n| Aspect | Path | Plan |\n|--------|------|------|\n| **Purpose** | Represents possible execution strategies (planning-time) | Represents actual executor instructions (runtime) |\n| **Cost info** | startup_cost, total_cost, rows | Copied from path |\n| **Selection** | Multiple paths exist; best one chosen | Single path selected and converted |\n| **Structure** | Recursive tree via parent RelOptInfo pointers | Recursive tree via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Key differences** | Focuses on cost estimates and ordering | Focuses on executor implementation |\n| **Children** | References via subpath or outer/innerjoinpath | Pointers via lefttree/righttree |\n| **Qualifications** | Implicit in WHERE/JOIN clauses | Explicit in qual lists |\n\n### 9. Important Upper-Level Planning\n\nThe planner also handles upper-level operations after the base join planning:\n\n- **GROUP BY:** `UPPERREL_GROUP_AGG`\n- **DISTINCT:** `UPPERREL_DISTINCT`\n- **ORDER BY:** `UPPERREL_ORDERED`\n- **Set operations:** `UPPERREL_SETOP` (UNION/INTERSECT/EXCEPT)\n- **Window functions:** `UPPERREL_WINDOW`\n\nThese are applied by `grouping_planner()` which generates additional paths for aggregation, sorting, etc., before the final path selection.\n\n### Summary\n\nThe PostgreSQL planner follows a clean two-phase architecture:\n\n1. **Phase 1 (Path Generation):** Explores the search space of possible execution strategies for each relation and join, generating multiple Path nodes that represent different ways to achieve the goal, annotated with cost estimates.\n\n2. **Phase 2 (Plan Creation):** Takes the best Path (minimizing startup or total cost depending on context) and converts it into an executable Plan tree that the executor can run, copying cost information and adding executor-specific details.\n\nThis separation allows the planner to:\n- Consider multiple strategies before committing to one\n- Apply sophisticated optimization rules during path generation\n- Avoid expensive plan conversions for dominated paths\n- Make cost-based decisions about which execution strategy to use"}],"totalDurationMs":80372,"totalTokens":75714,"totalToolUseCount":59,"usage":{"input_tokens":106,"cache_creation_input_tokens":966,"cache_read_input_tokens":71193,"output_tokens":3449,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":966,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}}}

Note that the flags will get modified\n    28→ * as they are passed down the plan tree, since an upper node may require\n    29→ * functionality in its subnode not demanded of the plan as a whole\n    30→ * (example: MergeJoin requires mark/restore capability in its inner input),\n    31→ * or an upper node may shield its input from some functionality requirement\n    32→ * (example: Materialize shields its input from needing to do backward scan).\n    33→ *\n    34→ * EXPLAIN_ONLY indicates that the plan tree is being initialized just so\n    35→ * EXPLAIN can print it out; it will not be run.  Hence, no side-effects\n    36→ * of startup should occur.  However, error checks (such as permission checks)\n    37→ * should be performed.\n    38→ *\n    39→ * EXPLAIN_GENERIC can only be used together with EXPLAIN_ONLY.  It indicates\n    40→ * that a generic plan is being shown using EXPLAIN (GENERIC_PLAN), which\n    41→ * means that missing parameter values must be tolerated.  Currently, the only\n    42→ * effect is to suppress execution-time partition pruning.\n    43→ *\n    44→ * REWIND indicates that the plan node should try to efficiently support\n    45→ * rescans without parameter changes.  (Nodes must support ExecReScan calls\n    46→ * in any case, but if this flag was not given, they are at liberty to do it\n    47→ * through complete recalculation.  Note that a parameter change forces a\n    48→ * full recalculation in any case.)\n    49→ *\n    50→ * BACKWARD indicates that the plan node must respect the es_direction flag.\n    51→ * When this is not passed, the plan node will only be run forwards.\n    52→ *\n    53→ * MARK indicates that the plan node must support Mark/Restore calls.\n    54→ * When this is not passed, no Mark/Restore will occur.\n    55→ *\n    56→ * SKIP_TRIGGERS tells ExecutorStart/ExecutorFinish to skip calling\n    57→ * AfterTriggerBeginQuery/AfterTriggerEndQuery.  This does not necessarily\n    58→ * mean that the plan can't queue any AFTER triggers; just that the caller\n    59→ * is responsible for there being a trigger context for them to be queued in.\n    60→ *\n    61→ * WITH_NO_DATA indicates that we are performing REFRESH MATERIALIZED VIEW\n    62→ * ... WITH NO DATA.  Currently, the only effect is to suppress errors about\n    63→ * scanning unpopulated materialized views.\n    64→ */\n    65→#define EXEC_FLAG_EXPLAIN_ONLY\t\t0x0001\t/* EXPLAIN, no ANALYZE */\n    66→#define EXEC_FLAG_EXPLAIN_GENERIC\t0x0002\t/* EXPLAIN (GENERIC_PLAN) */\n    67→#define EXEC_FLAG_REWIND\t\t\t0x0004\t/* need efficient rescan */\n    68→#define EXEC_FLAG_BACKWARD\t\t\t0x0008\t/* need backward scan */\n    69→#define EXEC_FLAG_MARK\t\t\t\t0x0010\t/* need mark/restore */\n    70→#define EXEC_FLAG_SKIP_TRIGGERS\t\t0x0020\t/* skip AfterTrigger setup */\n    71→#define EXEC_FLAG_WITH_NO_DATA\t\t0x0040\t/* REFRESH ... WITH NO DATA */\n    72→\n    73→\n    74→/* Hook for plugins to get control in ExecutorStart() */\n    75→typedef void (*ExecutorStart_hook_type) (QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags);\n    76→extern {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Vj2E7RDsp6Mmf3WC3rbDZ9","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→/*-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n     2→ *\n     3→ * tuptable.h\n     4→ *\t  tuple table support stuff\n     5→ *\n     6→ *\n     7→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1996-2025, PostgreSQL Global Development Group\n     8→ * Portions Copyright (c) 1994, Regents of the University of California\n     9→ *\n    10→ * src/include/executor/tuptable.h\n    11→ *\n    12→ *-------------------------------------------------------------------------\n    13→ */\n    14→#ifndef TUPTABLE_H\n    15→#define TUPTABLE_H\n    16→\n    17→#include \"access/htup.h\"\n    18→#include \"access/htup_details.h\"\n    19→#include \"access/sysattr.h\"\n    20→#include \"access/tupdesc.h\"\n    21→#include \"storage/buf.h\"\n    22→\n    23→/*----------\n    24→ * The executor stores tuples in a \"tuple table\" which is a List of\n    25→ * independent TupleTableSlots.\n    26→ *\n    27→ * There's various different types of tuple table slots, each being able to\n    28→ * store different types of tuples. Additional types of slots can be added\n    29→ * without modifying core code. The type of a slot is determined by the\n    30→ * TupleTableSlotOps* passed to the slot creation routine. The builtin types\n    31→ * of slots are\n    32→ *\n    33→ * 1. physical tuple in a disk buffer page (TTSOpsBufferHeapTuple)\n    34→ * 2. physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory (TTSOpsHeapTuple)\n    35→ * 3. \"minimal\" physical tuple constructed in palloc'ed memory\n    36→ *    (TTSOpsMinimalTuple)\n    37→ * 4. \"virtual\" tuple consisting of Datum/isnull arrays (TTSOpsVirtual)\n    38→ *\n    39→ *\n    40→ * The first two cases are similar in that they both deal with \"materialized\"\n    41→ * tuples, but resource management is different.  For a tuple in a disk page\n    42→ * we need to hold a pin on the buffer until the TupleTableSlot's reference\n    43→ * to the tuple is dropped; while for a palloc'd tuple we usually want the\n    44→ * tuple pfree'd when the TupleTableSlot's reference is dropped.\n    45→ *\n    46→ * A \"minimal\" tuple is handled similarly to a palloc'd regular tuple.\n    47→ * At present, minimal tuples never are stored in buffers, so there is no\n    48→ * parallel to case 1.  Note that a minimal tuple has no \"system columns\".\n    49→ *\n    50→ * A \"virtual\" tuple is an optimization used to minimize physical data copying\n    51→ * in a nest of plan nodes.  Until materialized pass-by-reference Datums in\n    52→ * the slot point to storage that is not directly associated with the\n    53→ * TupleTableSlot; generally they will point to part of a tuple stored in a\n    54→ * lower plan node's output TupleTableSlot, or to a function result\n    55→ * constructed in a plan node's per-tuple econtext.  It is the responsibility\n    56→ * of the generating plan node to be sure these resources are not released for\n    57→ * as long as the virtual tuple needs to be valid or is materialized.  Note\n    58→ * also that a virtual tuple does not have any \"system columns\".\n    59→ *\n    60→ * The Datum/isnull arrays of a TupleTableSlot serve double duty.  For virtual\n    61→ * slots they are the authoritative data.  For the other builtin slots,\n    62→ * the arrays contain data extracted from the tuple.  (In this state, any\n    63→ * pass-by-reference Datums point into the physical tuple.)  The extracted\n    64→ * information is built \"lazily\", ie, only as needed.  This serves to avoid\n    65→ * repeated extraction of data from the physical tuple.\n    66→ *\n    67→ * A TupleTableSlot can also be \"empty\", indicated by flag TTS_FLAG_EMPTY set\n    68→ * in tts_flags, holding no valid data.  This is the only valid state for a\n    69→ * freshly-created slot that has not yet had a tuple descriptor assigned to\n    70→ * it.  In this state, TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE should not be set in tts_flags and\n    71→ * tts_nvalid should be set to zero.\n    72→ *\n    73→ * The tupleDescriptor is simply referenced, not copied, by the TupleTableSlot\n    74→ * code.  The caller of ExecSetSlotDescriptor() is responsible for providing\n    75→ * a descriptor that will live as long as the slot does.  (Typically, both\n    76→ * slots and descriptors are in per-query memory and are freed by memory\n    77→ * context deallocation at query end; so it's not worth providing any extra\n    78→ * mechanism to do more.  However, the slot will increment the tupdesc\n    79→ * reference count if a reference-counted tupdesc is supplied.)\n    80→ *\n    81→ * When TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE is set in tts_flags, the physical tuple is \"owned\"\n    82→ * by the slot and should be freed when the slot's reference to the tuple is\n    83→ * dropped.\n    84→ *\n    85→ * tts_values/tts_isnull are allocated either when the slot is created (when\n    86→ * the descriptor is provided), or when a descriptor is assigned to the slot;\n    87→ * they are of length equal to the descriptor's natts.\n    88→ *\n    89→ * The TTS_FLAG_SLOW flag is saved state for\n    90→ * slot_deform_heap_tuple, and should not be touched by any other code.\n    91→ *----------\n    92→ */\n    93→\n    94→/* true = slot is empty */\n    95→#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_EMPTY\t\t\t(1 << 1)\n    96→#define TTS_EMPTY(slot)\t(((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_EMPTY) != 0)\n    97→\n    98→/* should pfree tuple \"owned\" by the slot? */\n    99→#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE\t\t(1 << 2)\n   100→#define TTS_SHOULDFREE(slot) (((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_SHOULDFREE) != 0)\n   101→\n   102→/* saved state for slot_deform_heap_tuple */\n   103→#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_SLOW\t\t(1 << 3)\n   104→#define TTS_SLOW(slot) (((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_SLOW) != 0)\n   105→\n   106→/* fixed tuple descriptor */\n   107→#define\t\t\tTTS_FLAG_FIXED\t\t(1 << 4)\n   108→#define TTS_FIXED(slot) (((slot)->tts_flags & TTS_FLAG_FIXED) != 0)\n   109→\n   110→struct TupleTableSlotOps;\n   111→typedef struct TupleTableSlotOps TupleTableSlotOps;\n   112→\n   113→/* base tuple table slot type */\n   114→typedef struct TupleTableSlot\n   115→{\n   116→\tNodeTag\t\ttype;\n   117→#define FIELDNO_TUPLETABLESLOT_FLAGS 1\n   118→\tuint16\t\ttts_flags;\t\t/* Boolean states */\n   119→#define FIELDNO_TUPLETABLESLOT_NVALID 2\n   120→\tAttrNumber\ttts_nvalid;\t\t/* # of valid values in tts_values */\n   121→\tconst TupleTableSlotOps *const tts_ops; /* implementation of slot */\n   122→#define FIELDNO_TUPLETABLESLOT_TUPLEDESCRIPTOR 4\n   123→\tTupleDesc\ttts_tupleDescriptor;\t/* slot's tuple descriptor */\n   124→#define FIELDNO_TUPLETABLESLOT_VALUES 5\n   125→\tDatum\t   *tts_values;\t\t/* current per-attribute values */\n   126→#define FIELDNO_TUPLETABLESLOT_ISNULL 6\n   127→\tbool\t   *tts_isnull;\t\t/* current per-attribute isnull flags */\n   128→\tMemoryContext tts_mcxt;\t\t/* slot itself is in this context */\n   129→\tItemPointerData tts_tid;\t/* stored tuple's tid */\n   130→\tOid\t\t\ttts_tableOid;\t/* table oid of tuple */\n   131→} TupleTableSlot;\n   132→\n   133→/* routines for a TupleTableSlot implementation */\n   134→struct TupleTableSlotOps\n   135→{\n   136→\t/* Minimum size of the slot */\n   137→\tsize_t\t\tbase_slot_size;\n   138→\n   139→\t/* Initialization. */\n   140→\tvoid\t\t(*init) (TupleTableSlot *slot);\n   141→\n   142→\t/* Destruction. */\n   143→\tvoid\t\t(*release) (TupleTableSlot *slot);\n   144→\n   145→\t/*\n   146→\t * Clear the contents of the slot. If no projection is necessary\n  1226→\t * ExecConditionalAssignProjectionInfo() defaults those fields to the scan\n  1227→\t * operations.\n  1228→\t */\n  1229→\tconst TupleTableSlotOps *scanops;\n  1230→\tconst TupleTableSlotOps *outerops;\n  1231→\tconst TupleTableSlotOps *innerops;\n  1232→\tconst TupleTableSlotOps *resultops;\n  1233→\tbool\t\tscanopsfixed;\n  1234→\tbool\t\touteropsfixed;\n  1235→\tbool\t\tinneropsfixed;\n  1236→\tbool\t\tresultopsfixed;\n  1237→\tbool\t\tscanopsset;\n  1238→\tbool\t\touteropsset;\n  1239→\tbool\t\tinneropsset;\n  1240→\tbool\t\tresultopsset;\n  1241→} PlanState;\n  1242→\n  1243→/* ----------------\n  1244→ *\tthese are defined to avoid confusion problems with \"left\"\n  1245→ *\tand \"right\" and \"inner\" and \"outer\".  The convention is that\n  1246→ *\tthe \"left\" plan is the \"outer\" plan and the \"right\" plan is\n  1247→ *\tthe inner plan, but these make the code more readable.\n  1248→ * ----------------\n  1249→ */\n  1250→#define innerPlanState(node)\t\t(((PlanState *)(node))->righttree)\n  1251→#define outerPlanState(node)\t\t(((PlanState *)(node))->lefttree)\n  1252→\n  1253→/* Macros for inline access to certain instrumentation counters */\n  1254→#define InstrCountTuples2(node, delta) \\\n  1255→\tdo { \\\n  1256→\t\tif (((PlanState *)(node))->instrument) \\\n  1257→\t\t\t((PlanState *)(node))->instrument->ntuples2 += (delta); \\\n  1258→\t} while (0)\n  1259→#define InstrCountFiltered1(node, delta) \\\n  1260→\tdo { \\\n  1261→\t\tif (((PlanState *)(node))->instrument) \\\n  1262→\t\t\t((PlanState *)(node))->instrument->nfiltered1 += (delta); \\\n  1263→\t} while(0)\n  1264→#define InstrCountFiltered2(node, delta) \\\n  1265→\tdo { \\\n  1266→\t\tif (((PlanState *)(node))->instrument) \\\n  1267→\t\t\t((PlanState *)(node))->instrument->nfiltered2 += (delta); \\\n  1268→\t} while(0)\n  1269→\n  1270→/*\n  1271→ * EPQState is state for executing an EvalPlanQual recheck on a candidate\n  1272→ * tuples e.g. in ModifyTable or LockRows.\n  1273→ *\n  1274→ * To execute EPQ a separate EState is created (stored in ->recheckestate),\n  1275→ * which shares some resources, like the rangetable, with the main query's\n  1276→ * EState (stored in ->parentestate). The (sub-)tree of the plan that needs to\n  1277→ * be rechecked (in ->plan), is separately initialized (into\n  1278→ * ->recheckplanstate), but shares plan nodes with the corresponding nodes in\n  1279→ * the main query. The scan nodes in that separate executor tree are changed\n  1280→ * to return only the current tuple of interest for the respective\n  1281→ * table. Those tuples are either provided by the caller (using\n  1282→ * EvalPlanQualSlot), and/or found using the rowmark mechanism (non-locking\n  1283→ * rowmarks by the EPQ machinery itself, locking ones by the caller).\n  1284→ *\n  1285→ * While the plan to be checked may be changed using EvalPlanQualSetPlan(),\n  1286→ * all such plans need to share the same EState.\n  1287→ */\n  1288→typedef struct EPQState\n  1289→{\n  1290→\t/* These are initialized by EvalPlanQualInit() and do not change later: */\n  1291→\tEState\t   *parentestate;\t/* main query's EState */\n  1292→\tint\t\t\tepqParam;\t\t/* ID of Param to force scan node re-eval */\n  1293→\tList\t   *resultRelations;\t/* integer list of RT indexes, or NIL */\n  1294→\n  1295→\t/*\n  1296→\t * relsubs_slot[scanrelid - 1] holds the EPQ test tuple to be returned by\n  1297→\t * the scan node for the scanrelid'th RT index, in place of performing an\n  1298→\t * actual table scan. Let me compile a comprehensive report on the PostgreSQL executor architecture.\n\n## PostgreSQL Executor Architecture: The Volcano-Style Tuple Execution Model\n\nBased on my analysis of the PostgreSQL codebase (version 18.2), here's a comprehensive explanation of how the Volcano-style tuple execution model works:\n\n---\n\n### 1. EXECUTOR ENTRY POINTS\n\n#### **ExecutorStart() - Initialize Execution**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 121-264)\n\n```c\nvoid\nExecutorStart(QueryDesc *queryDesc, int eflags)\n{\n    if (ExecutorStart_hook)\n        (*ExecutorStart_hook) (queryDesc, eflags);\n    else\n        standard_ExecutorStart(queryDesc, eflags);\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n1. Creates an `EState` (execution state) - the global context for execution\n2. Sets up memory contexts for the query\n3. Calls `InitPlan()` which recursively initializes the plan tree via `ExecInitNode()`\n4. Creates expression contexts for evaluating predicates\n5. Registers the snapshot for tuple visibility\n6. Sets up AFTER triggers if needed\n\nThe `EState` structure holds:\n- `es_direction` - scan direction (forward/backward)\n- `es_snapshot` - transaction visibility snapshot\n- `es_tupleTable` - list of tuple table slots\n- `es_processed` - count of tuples processed\n- `es_query_cxt` - memory context for the query\n- `es_per_tuple_exprcontext` - context for evaluating expressions per tuple\n\n#### **ExecutorRun() - Execute the Plan**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 296-389)\n\n```c\nvoid\nstandard_ExecutorRun(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n                     ScanDirection direction, uint64 count)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    ...\n    \n    if (!ScanDirectionIsNoMovement(direction))\n        ExecutePlan(queryDesc, operation, sendTuples, count, direction, dest);\n    \n    estate->es_total_processed += estate->es_processed;\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n- Calls `ExecutePlan()` which is the main tuple iteration loop\n- Can be called multiple times to fetch tuples incrementally\n- Sends tuples to the destination receiver (e.g., network socket, client)\n\n#### **ExecutorFinish() - Finalize Execution**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 414-449)\n\n```c\nvoid\nstandard_ExecutorFinish(QueryDesc *queryDesc)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    \n    ExecPostprocessPlan(estate);  // Run ModifyTable to completion\n    \n    if (!(estate->es_top_eflags & EXEC_FLAG_SKIP_TRIGGERS))\n        AfterTriggerEndQuery(estate);  // Execute AFTER triggers\n}\n```\n\n**What happens:**\n- Runs any remaining ModifyTable operations\n- Executes queued AFTER triggers\n- Must be called after the last ExecutorRun() call\n\n---\n\n### 2. THE VOLCANO-STYLE DISPATCH MECHANISM: ExecProcNode\n\n#### **The ExecProcNode Macro/Inline Function**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/executor.h` (lines 308-316)\n\n```c\n/* ----------------------------------------------------------------\n *\t\tExecProcNode\n *\n *\t\tExecute the given node to return a(nother) tuple.\n * ----------------------------------------------------------------\n */\n#ifndef FRONTEND\nstatic inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNode(PlanState *node)\n{\n    if (node->chgParam != NULL) /* something changed? */\n        ExecReScan(node);       /* let ReScan handle this */\n\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);\n}\n#endif\n```\n\n**Key insight:** This is the heart of the Volcano model. Rather than dispatching based on node type via a switch statement, each node has a **function pointer** (`ExecProcNode`) that points to its specific execution function. This is:\n- More flexible (allows dynamic dispatch)\n- Less branchy (better CPU cache performance)\n- Allows runtime optimization (functions can be swapped in/out)\n\n#### **Node-Type Specific Dispatch During Initialization**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` (lines 141-420)\n\nThe `ExecInitNode()` function creates the appropriate PlanState for each node type:\n\n```c\nPlanState *\nExecInitNode(Plan *node, EState *estate, int eflags)\n{\n    PlanState *result;\n    \n    switch (nodeTag(node))\n    {\n        case T_SeqScan:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitSeqScan((SeqScan *) node,\n                                                   estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        case T_NestLoop:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitNestLoop((NestLoop *) node,\n                                                    estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        case T_HashJoin:\n            result = (PlanState *) ExecInitHashJoin((HashJoin *) node,\n                                                    estate, eflags);\n            break;\n        // ... many more node types\n    }\n\n    ExecSetExecProcNode(result, result->ExecProcNode);\n    return result;\n}\n```\n\nAfter initialization, the result PlanState has `ExecProcNode` set to the appropriate function for that node type.\n\n#### **Wrapper Function for First Call and Instrumentation**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execProcnode.c` (lines 447-490)\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNodeFirst(PlanState *node)\n{\n    /* Check stack depth once during first call */\n    check_stack_depth();\n\n    /* Switch to the appropriate wrapper based on instrumentation needs */\n    if (node->instrument)\n        node->ExecProcNode = ExecProcNodeInstr;\n    else\n        node->ExecProcNode = node->ExecProcNodeReal;\n\n    return node->ExecProcNode(node);\n}\n\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecProcNodeInstr(PlanState *node)\n{\n    TupleTableSlot *result;\n\n    InstrStartNode(node->instrument);\n    result = node->ExecProcNodeReal(node);\n    InstrStopNode(node->instrument, TupIsNull(result) ? 0.0 : 1.0);\n\n    return result;\n}\n```\n\nThis pattern allows for cheap dynamic dispatch: after the first call, the function pointer is updated to skip unnecessary wrapper logic.\n\n---\n\n### 3. THE MAIN EXECUTION LOOP: ExecutePlan\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/execMain.c` (lines 1659-1773)\n\n```c\nstatic void\nExecutePlan(QueryDesc *queryDesc,\n            CmdType operation,\n            bool sendTuples,\n            uint64 numberTuples,\n            ScanDirection direction,\n            DestReceiver *dest)\n{\n    EState *estate = queryDesc->estate;\n    PlanState *planstate = queryDesc->planstate;\n    TupleTableSlot *slot;\n    uint64 current_tuple_count;\n\n    /*\n     * Loop until we've processed the proper number of tuples from the plan.\n     */\n    for (;;)\n    {\n        /* Reset the per-output-tuple exprcontext */\n        ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate);\n\n        /*\n         * Execute the plan and obtain a tuple\n         */\n        slot = ExecProcNode(planstate);  // <-- THE VOLCANO PULL\n\n        /*\n         * if the tuple is null, then we assume there is nothing more to\n         * process so we just end the loop...\n         */\n        if (TupIsNull(slot))\n            break;\n\n        /*\n         * If we have a junk filter, then project a new tuple with the junk\n         * removed.\n         */\n        if (estate->es_junkFilter != NULL)\n            slot = ExecFilterJunk(estate->es_junkFilter, slot);\n\n        /*\n         * If we are supposed to send the tuple somewhere, do so.\n         */\n        if (sendTuples)\n        {\n            if (!dest->receiveSlot(slot, dest))\n                break;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Count tuples processed, if this is a SELECT.\n         */\n        if (operation == CMD_SELECT)\n            (estate->es_processed)++;\n\n        /*\n         * check our tuple count.. if we've processed the proper number then\n         * quit, else loop again and process more tuples.  Zero numberTuples\n         * means no limit.\n         */\n        current_tuple_count++;\n        if (numberTuples && numberTuples == current_tuple_count)\n            break;\n    }\n\n    /*\n     * If we know we won't need to back up, we can release resources at this\n     * point.\n     */\n    if (!(estate->es_top_eflags & EXEC_FLAG_BACKWARD))\n        ExecShutdownNode(planstate);\n}\n```\n\n**Key insight:** The **Volcano pull model** works like this:\n1. The top-level node (usually a select operator) calls `ExecProcNode()`\n2. This recursively pulls tuples from child nodes\n3. Tuples flow back up the tree as TupleTableSlots\n4. When a node returns a NULL slot, the iterator is exhausted\n\n---\n\n### 4. EXAMPLE: How a Nested Loop Join Works\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/nodeNestloop.c` (lines 59-200)\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecNestLoop(PlanState *pstate)\n{\n    NestLoopState *node = castNode(NestLoopState, pstate);\n    PlanState *innerPlan = innerPlanState(node);\n    PlanState *outerPlan = outerPlanState(node);\n    \n    for (;;)\n    {\n        /* If we don't have an outer tuple, get the next one */\n        if (node->nl_NeedNewOuter)\n        {\n            /*\n             * This calls the outer plan's ExecProcNode function\n             * (e.g., ExecSeqScan if the outer plan is a SeqScan)\n             */\n            outerTupleSlot = ExecProcNode(outerPlan);\n\n            if (TupIsNull(outerTupleSlot))\n                return NULL;  /* No more outer tuples */\n\n            /* Store outer tuple and rescan inner plan */\n            econtext->ecxt_outertuple = outerTupleSlot;\n            ExecReScan(innerPlan);\n            node->nl_NeedNewOuter = false;\n        }\n\n        /*\n         * Get next inner tuple\n         * This calls the inner plan's ExecProcNode function\n         */\n        innerTupleSlot = ExecProcNode(innerPlan);\n        econtext->ecxt_innertuple = innerTupleSlot;\n\n        if (TupIsNull(innerTupleSlot))\n        {\n            /* No more inner tuples for this outer tuple */\n            node->nl_NeedNewOuter = true;\n\n            /* Handle outer joins (LEFT/ANTI) */\n            if (!node->nl_MatchedOuter &&\n                (node->js.jointype == JOIN_LEFT ||\n                 node->js.jointype == JOIN_ANTI))\n            {\n                econtext->ecxt_innertuple = node->nl_NullInnerTupleSlot;\n\n                if (otherqual == NULL || ExecQual(otherqual, econtext))\n                    return ExecProject(node->js.ps.ps_ProjInfo);\n            }\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        /* Check join condition */\n        if (ExecQual(joinqual, econtext))\n        {\n            /* Qualification succeeded, apply projection and return */\n            return ExecProject(node->js.ps.ps_ProjInfo);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Tuple flow diagram:**\n```\nExecutePlan() [Main loop]\n    |\n    v\nExecProcNode(NestLoopState)\n    |\n    +---> ExecProcNode(OuterPlanState)  [e.g., SeqScan]\n    |         |\n    |         v\n    |     Get tuple from table\n    |     [return slot1]\n    |\n    +---> Store in ecxt_outertuple\n    |\n    +---> ExecProcNode(InnerPlanState)  [e.g., SeqScan]\n    |         |\n    |         v\n    |     Get tuple from table\n    |     [return slot2]\n    |\n    +---> Check join condition on (slot1, slot2)\n    |\n    +---> Apply projection\n    |\n    v\n    [return result slot]\n```\n\n---\n\n### 5. EXAMPLE: How Sequential Scan Works\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/backend/executor/nodeSeqscan.c` (lines 206-280)\n\nThe SeqScan node initializes different ExecProcNode variants based on the presence of qualifications and projections:\n\n```c\nSeqScanState *\nExecInitSeqScan(SeqScan *node, EState *estate, int eflags)\n{\n    SeqScanState *scanstate;\n    \n    scanstate = makeNode(SeqScanState);\n    \n    /* Open the scan relation */\n    scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation =\n        ExecOpenScanRelation(estate,\n                             node->scan.scanrelid,\n                             eflags);\n\n    /* Create slot for tuples from the table */\n    ExecInitScanTupleSlot(estate, &scanstate->ss,\n                          RelationGetDescr(scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation),\n                          table_slot_callbacks(scanstate->ss.ss_currentRelation));\n\n    /* Initialize qual (WHERE clause) */\n    scanstate->ss.ps.qual =\n        ExecInitQual(node->scan.plan.qual, (PlanState *) scanstate);\n\n    /* Choose the right variant based on qual and projection */\n    if (scanstate->ss.ps.state->es_epq_active != NULL)\n        scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanEPQ;\n    else if (scanstate->ss.ps.qual == NULL)\n    {\n        if (scanstate->ss.ps.ps_ProjInfo == NULL)\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScan;\n        else\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithProject;\n    }\n    else\n    {\n        if (scanstate->ss.ps.ps_ProjInfo == NULL)\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithQual;\n        else\n            scanstate->ss.ps.ExecProcNode = ExecSeqScanWithQualProject;\n    }\n\n    return scanstate;\n}\n```\n\n**The basic SeqScan function:**\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nExecSeqScan(PlanState *pstate)\n{\n    SeqScanState *node = castNode(SeqScanState, pstate);\n\n    return ExecScanExtended(&node->ss,\n                            (ExecScanAccessMtd) SeqNext,\n                            (ExecScanRecheckMtd) SeqRecheck,\n                            NULL,   /* no EPQ */\n                            NULL,   /* no qual */\n                            NULL);  /* no projection */\n}\n```\n\n**The SeqNext function** (access method):\n\n```c\nstatic TupleTableSlot *\nSeqNext(SeqScanState *node)\n{\n    TableScanDesc scandesc = node->ss.ss_currentScanDesc;\n    EState *estate = node->ss.ps.state;\n    TupleTableSlot *slot = node->ss.ss_ScanTupleSlot;\n\n    if (scandesc == NULL)\n    {\n        /* Begin the scan */\n        scandesc = table_beginscan(node->ss.ss_currentRelation,\n                                   estate->es_snapshot,\n                                   0, NULL);\n        node->ss.ss_currentScanDesc = scandesc;\n    }\n\n    /* Get the next tuple from the table */\n    if (table_scan_getnextslot(scandesc, estate->es_direction, slot))\n        return slot;  /* Return the slot with the tuple */\n    \n    return NULL;  /* End of scan */\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6. QUALIFICATION AND PROJECTION: ExecScanExtended\n\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/execScan.h` (lines 159-252)\n\nThis inline function handles the common pattern of:\n1. Fetching a tuple from the table\n2. Checking the WHERE clause (qual)\n3. Applying the SELECT list (projection)\n\n```c\nstatic pg_attribute_always_inline TupleTableSlot *\nExecScanExtended(ScanState *node,\n                 ExecScanAccessMtd accessMtd,\n                 ExecScanRecheckMtd recheckMtd,\n                 EPQState *epqstate,\n                 ExprState *qual,\n                 ProjectionInfo *projInfo)\n{\n    ExprContext *econtext = node->ps.ps_ExprContext;\n\n    ResetExprContext(econtext);\n\n    /*\n     * Main scanning loop:\n     * 1. Fetch tuple from table\n     * 2. Check WHERE clause\n     * 3. Apply projection (SELECT list)\n     */\n    for (;;)\n    {\n        TupleTableSlot *slot;\n\n        /* Step 1: Fetch next tuple */\n        slot = ExecScanFetch(node, epqstate, accessMtd, recheckMtd);\n\n        if (TupIsNull(slot))\n        {\n            /* No more tuples */\n            if (projInfo)\n                return ExecClearTuple(projInfo->pi_state.resultslot);\n            else\n                return slot;\n        }\n\n        /* Step 2: Place tuple in context and check WHERE clause */\n        econtext->ecxt_scantuple = slot;\n\n        if (qual == NULL || ExecQual(qual, econtext))\n        {\n            /* Tuple passes the WHERE clause */\n            if (projInfo)\n            {\n                /* Step 3: Apply projection and return result */\n                return ExecProject(projInfo);\n            }\n            else\n            {\n                /* No projection needed, return raw scan tuple */\n                return slot;\n            }\n        }\n        else\n        {\n            /* Tuple failed WHERE clause, count it and try next */\n            InstrCountFiltered1(node, 1);\n            ResetExprContext(econtext);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Example:** For `SELECT col1, col2 FROM table WHERE col3 > 10`:\n- `accessMtd` = `SeqNext` - fetches raw tuples from table\n- `qual` = Expression for `col3 > 10`\n- `projInfo` = Projection for `col1, col2`\n\n**Tuple flow:**\n```\nLoop:\n  1. SeqNext() -> [col1=1, col2=2, col3=15, ...]  (slot)\n  2. econtext->ecxt_scantuple = slot\n  3. ExecQual(qual, econtext):\n       - Evaluates col3 > 10 using slot values\n       - Returns true if 15 > 10\n  4. ExecProject(projInfo):\n       - Builds new tuple with only col1, col2\n       - Returns [col1=1, col2=2] in result slot\n```\n\n---\n\n### 7. KEY DATA STRUCTURES\n\n#### **PlanState - Runtime State for a Plan Node**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 1149-1241)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct PlanState\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n\n    Plan *plan;              /* associated Plan node */\n    EState *state;           /* execution state */\n\n    ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNode;      /* function to return next tuple */\n    ExecProcNodeMtd ExecProcNodeReal;  /* actual function if above is wrapper */\n\n    Instrumentation *instrument;  /* runtime statistics */\n    WorkerInstrumentation *worker_instrument;\n\n    /* Common structural data */\n    ExprState *qual;                    /* boolean qual condition (WHERE) */\n    struct PlanState *lefttree;         /* outer child */\n    struct PlanState *righttree;        /* inner child */\n\n    List *initPlan;          /* Init SubPlanState nodes */\n    List *subPlan;           /* SubPlanState nodes in expressions */\n\n    Bitmapset *chgParam;     /* set of IDs of changed parameters */\n\n    TupleDesc ps_ResultTupleDesc;       /* node's return type */\n    TupleTableSlot *ps_ResultTupleSlot; /* slot for result tuples */\n    ExprContext *ps_ExprContext;        /* expression evaluation context */\n    ProjectionInfo *ps_ProjInfo;        /* projection (SELECT list) */\n\n    bool async_capable;\n    TupleDesc scandesc;\n\n    /* Slot type information for optimization */\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *scanops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *outerops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *innerops;\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *resultops;\n    /* ... and flags for which are fixed/set ... */\n} PlanState;\n```\n\n#### **TupleTableSlot - How Tuples are Passed Between Operators**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/executor/tuptable.h` (lines 93-226)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct TupleTableSlot\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n    uint16 tts_flags;        /* Boolean states */\n    AttrNumber tts_nvalid;   /* # of valid values in tts_values */\n    const TupleTableSlotOps *const tts_ops;  /* slot type operations */\n    TupleDesc tts_tupleDescriptor;           /* slot's tuple descriptor */\n    Datum *tts_values;       /* current per-attribute values (lazily filled) */\n    bool *tts_isnull;        /* current per-attribute isnull flags */\n    MemoryContext tts_mcxt;  /* slot's memory context */\n    ItemPointerData tts_tid; /* tuple's ID (for physical tuples) */\n    Oid tts_tableOid;        /* table OID */\n} TupleTableSlot;\n```\n\n**Slot types:**\n1. **Virtual slots** (`TTSOpsVirtual`) - Datum/isnull arrays only, no physical tuple\n   - Fastest, minimal memory overhead\n   - Data points into parent slot's memory\n2. **Heap tuples** (`TTSOpsHeapTuple`) - Palloc'd physical tuple\n   - Used when tuple must outlive parent slot\n3. **Minimal tuples** (`TTSOpsMinimalTuple`) - Compact physical tuple without system columns\n   - Used for sorting/hashing\n4. **Buffer heap tuples** (`TTSOpsBufferHeapTuple`) - Tuple in buffer page with pin\n   - Used for heap scans\n\n**Key macro:**\n```c\n#define TupIsNull(slot) \\\n    ((slot) == NULL || TTS_EMPTY(slot))\n```\n\n#### **ExprContext - Expression Evaluation Context**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 262-314)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct ExprContext\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n\n    /* Tuples that Var nodes may refer to */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_scantuple;  /* scan tuple */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_innertuple; /* inner join tuple */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_outertuple; /* outer join tuple */\n\n    /* Memory contexts for expression evaluation */\n    MemoryContext ecxt_per_query_memory;  /* long-lived */\n    MemoryContext ecxt_per_tuple_memory;  /* reset each tuple */\n\n    /* Parameter values */\n    ParamExecData *ecxt_param_exec_vals;\n    ParamListInfo ecxt_param_list_info;\n\n    /* Aggregate/window function values */\n    Datum *ecxt_aggvalues;\n    bool *ecxt_aggnulls;\n\n    /* OLD/NEW tuples for triggers */\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_oldtuple;\n    TupleTableSlot *ecxt_newtuple;\n\n    EState *ecxt_estate;\n    ExprContext_CB *ecxt_callbacks;\n} ExprContext;\n```\n\nWhen evaluating an expression like `col1 > col2`, the executor:\n1. Sets `ecxt_scantuple` to the current tuple slot\n2. Calls the expression's evalfunc\n3. Expression reads values from the slot via `slot_getattr()`\n\n#### **ExprState - Compiled Expression State**\n**File:** `/workspace/src/include/nodes/execnodes.h` (lines 86-150)\n\n```c\ntypedef struct ExprState\n{\n    NodeTag type;\n    uint8 flags;\n\n    /* Result storage */\n    bool resnull;\n    Datum resvalue;\n\n    /* If projecting a tuple result */\n    TupleTableSlot *resultslot;\n\n    /* Evaluation instructions */\n    struct ExprEvalStep *steps;\n\n    /* The evaluation function */\n    ExprStateEvalFunc evalfunc;\n\n    /* Original expression for debugging */\n    Expr *expr;\n\n    void *evalfunc_private;\n    \n    int steps_len;\n    int steps_alloc;\n\n    struct PlanState *parent;\n    ParamListInfo ext_params;\n\n    Datum *innermost_caseval;\n    bool *innermost_casenull;\n\n    Datum *innermost_domainval;\n    bool *innermost_domainnull;\n\n    ErrorSaveContext *escontext;\n} ExprState;\n```\n\n---\n\n### 8. THE TUPLE FLOW MODEL: Complete Example\n\n**Query:** `SELECT a.x, b.y FROM a JOIN b ON a.id = b.aid WHERE a.x > 10 LIMIT 5`\n\n**Plan tree:**\n```\nLimit (5)\n  |\n  NestLoop (JOIN ON a.id = b.aid)\n    |\n    +-- SeqScan a (WHERE a.x > 10)\n    |\n    +-- IndexScan b (WHERE b.aid = a.id)\n```\n\n**Tuple flow:**\n\n```\nExecutePlan() main loop:\n{\n    ResetPerTupleExprContext(estate)\n    \n    slot = ExecProcNode(LimitState)\n    \n    LimitState->ExecProcNode(LimitState):\n    {\n        if (count >= 5) return NULL;\n        \n        slot = ExecProcNode(NestLoopState)\n        \n        NestLoopState->ExecProcNode(NestLoopState):\n        {\n            for (;;) {\n                if (need_new_outer) {\n                    outer_slot = ExecProcNode(SeqScanState_a)\n                    \n                    SeqScanState_a->ExecProcNode(SeqScanState_a):\n                    {\n                        // Loop until we find a tuple where x > 10\n                        for (;;) {\n                            raw_slot = SeqNext(a)  // Get from table\n                            if (TupIsNull(raw_slot)) return NULL;\n                            \n                            econtext->ecxt_scantuple = raw_slot\n                            \n                            if (ExecQual(qual: a.x > 10, econtext)) {\n                                // Qual passed\n                                return ExecProject(projection: a.x, a.id)\n                                // Returns slot with [x=15, id=3]\n                            }\n                            // Qual failed, loop again\n                        }\n                    }\n                    \n                    if (TupIsNull(outer_slot)) return NULL;  // End of a\n                    \n                    econtext->ecxt_outertuple = outer_slot  // [x=15, id=3]\n                    ExecReScan(IndexScanState_b)  // Rescan b for new id\n                }\n                \n                inner_slot = ExecProcNode(IndexScanState_b)\n                \n                IndexScanState_b->ExecProcNode(IndexScanState_b):\n                {\n                    // Get next b tuple where b.aid = 3\n                    raw_slot = IndexNext(b, key: aid=3)\n                    if (TupIsNull(raw_slot)) return NULL;\n                    \n                    return ExecProject(projection: b.y)\n                    // Returns slot with [y=99]\n                }\n                \n                if (TupIsNull(inner_slot)) {\n                    need_new_outer = true;\n                    continue;  // Back to top, get next outer\n                }\n                \n                econtext->ecxt_innertuple = inner_slot  // [y=99]\n                \n                // Join quals already checked by index scan\n                // Apply projection: SELECT a.x, b.y\n                return ExecProject(projection: a.x, b.y)\n                // Returns slot with [x=15, y=99]\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if (TupIsNull(slot)) return NULL;\n        count++;\n        return slot  // [x=15, y=99]\n    }\n    \n    if (TupIsNull(slot)) break;  // End of results\n    \n    receiveSlot(slot, dest)  // Send to client\n    \n    count++\n}\n```\n\n**Key observations:**\n1. **Pull-based:** Each node calls its children to get tuples\n2. **Lazy evaluation:** Tuples only fetched when needed\n3. **Iterator protocol:** NULL slot signals end of stream\n4. **Context passing:** ExprContext passes tuples to expressions\n5. **Slot reuse:** Tuples passed via slot pointers, not copied\n6. **Qual checking:** WHERE clauses evaluated early in the pipeline\n\n---\n\n### 9. OPTIMIZATION: Virtual Slots and Lazy Materialization\n\nPostgreSQL optimizes the Volcano model by:\n\n1. **Virtual Slots** - Don't materialize tuples; just keep Datum/isnull arrays\n   - Projection creates virtual tuple from expressions\n   - Child slot's Datums referenced directly\n   - No copy until necessary\n\n2. **Lazy Deformation** - Don't extract tuple attributes until needed\n   - `slot_getsomeattrs()` only extracts needed attributes\n   - Saves CPU and memory\n\n3. **Function Pointer Swapping** - Choose the fastest path for each case\n   - ExecSeqScan (no qual, no proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithQual (qual, no proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithProject (no qual, proj)\n   - ExecSeqScanWithQualProject (qual and proj)\n\n4. **Instrumentation** - Track performance with minimal overhead\n   - ExecProcNodeFirst sets up instrumentation on first call\n   - Then points directly to ExecProcNodeInstr or actual function\n\n---\n\n### Summary\n\nThe Volcano-style executor in PostgreSQL works through:\n\n1. **Initialization phase** - `ExecutorStart()` recursively initializes plan tree, creating PlanState for each node\n2. **Execution phase** - `ExecutorRun()` calls `ExecutePlan()` which pulls tuples from root node\n3. **Pull-based iteration** - Each node calls its children via function pointers to get tuples\n4. **Iterator protocol** - NULL slot signals end of stream\n5. **Context threading** - ExprContext passes tuple references through the expression evaluator\n6. **Lazy evaluation** - Qualifications checked and projections applied as tuples flow up tree\n7. **Slot abstraction** - Different slot types for different tuple representations (virtual, heap, minimal, etc.)\n8. **Dynamic dispatch** - Function pointers allow runtime selection of optimal code paths\n9. **Memory management** - Per-tuple memory context reset between iterations to prevent leaks\n\nThis elegant design balances flexibility, performance, and memory efficiency."},{"type":"text","text":"agentId: aadf5a818693bd058 (for resuming to continue this agent's work if needed)\n<usage>total_tokens: 82959\ntool_uses: 42\nduration_ms: 127757</usage>"}]}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"026159cb-0c93-4594-8106-2a09e233cb62","uuid":"f9eb865d-1a7d-46f3-a9d9-4247056b7ffe","tool_use_result":{"status":"completed","prompt":"I need to understand the PostgreSQL executor architecture, specifically the Volcano-style tuple execution model.
